DEPARTMENT OF TRANSPORTATION
FEDERAL MOTOR CARRIER SAFETY ADMINISTRATION
REGISTER

A Daily Summary of Motor Carrier Applications and of Decisions and Notices Issued by the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration.
Decisions and Notices Released Jul 03, 2025 -- 10:30 A.M.
Notice
Please note the timeframe required to revoke a motor carrier's operating authority for failing to have sufficient levels of insurance on file is a 33 day process. The process will only allow a carrier to hold operating authority without insurance reflected on our Licensing and Insurance database for up to three (3) days. Revocation decisions will be tied to our enforcement program which will focus on the operations of uninsured carriers. This process will further ensure that the public is adequately protected in case of a motor carrier crash. Accordingly, we are adopting the following procedure for revocation of authority; 1) The first notice will go out three (3) days after FMCSA receives notification from the insurance company that the carrier's policy will be cancelled in 30 days. This notification informs the carrier that it must provide evidence that it is in full compliance with FMCSA's insurance regulations within 30 days. 2) If the carrier has not complied with FMCSA's insurance requirements after 30 days, a final decision revoking the operating authority will be issued.

TRANSFERS
Small Carrier Transfer Applications
Involving Motor Carriers, Property Brokers, Freight Forwarders, and Holders of Certificates of Registration
AGENCY: Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration.

ACTION: The FMCSA has approved, subject to public comment, the transfer of authority of motor carriers, property brokers, freight forwarders, and holders of certificates of registration, pursuant to the decision in Ex Parte No. MC 111 (Sub No. 1), Transfer Rules, 4 I.C.C.2d 382, (1988), and the regulations at 49 CFR Part 365, Subpart D.

The parties may consummate a proposed transaction at any time 10 days after the filing of the application.

Protests may be filed within 20 days of the publication date of the application. If a protest is received, the FMCSA will issue a decision disposing of the protest, and any transaction consummated prior to the FMCSA decision will be at the parties' own risk, subject to any conditions that the FMCSA may impose subsequently.

Similarly, if either party has a less-than-satisfactory safety rating, consummation of the transaction pursuant to the 10-day rule is at the parties' own risk, subject to any conditions that the FMCSA may impose subsequently.

If no protests are received, or if the FMCSA does not issue a subsequent decision on safety grounds, the publication of the application will become the final action of the FMCSA.

(1) motor carriers: insurance (49 CFR 1043) (liability: Form BMC-91 or BMC-91X; cargo: Form BMC 34); designation of process agents (49 CFR 1044)
(Form BOC-3); and tariffs (49 CFR 1312); or

General Information

GRANT DECISION NOTICES:	Permanent motor carrier, broker, and freight forwarder authority applications filed on or after January 1, 1995.

FMCSA Licensing and Insurance Register

The following requests for authority have been reviewed by the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (hereafter, the Administration) and are being published as preliminary grants. Some descriptions of requested service may have been modified to provide for consistency in authorities issued by the Administration. These grant decision notices do not represent authority to operate.

Amendments to the applications are generally not permitted. Once the application has been filed, the applicant may revise a request for authority or supplement evidence only with the approval of the Administration.

Applicants will be sent a letter on the day when notice of their application appears in the FMCSA Register. This letter informs them of their docket number, their insurance and process agent filing requirements and deadlines, and the publication date in the Register.

Legally sufficient opposition in the form of verified statements must be filed within 10 days from date of publication.

In the absence of opposition, authorities will be issued to those applicants that, within 20 days from date of publication, have filed evidence of appropriate compliance.

Applications that are not supplemented with the required insurance and process agent filings by the 20th day following publication in the FMCSA Register will be dismissed. Dismissal notices will be issued to non-complying applicants on the 30th day after publication in the FMCSA Register.

Authorities will remain in full effect only as long as the applicant maintains appropriate compliance.

Please direct inquiries about the status of motor carrier applications and insurance filings to the Automated Response Capability telephone system, at (202) 358-7000 or to our web site at http://li-public.fmcsa.dot.gov.

Please direct inquiries about revocation notices to the Section of Insurance, at (202) 385-2423 M-F 8:00 AM - 4:30 PM EST or (202) 385-2400 after hours and holidays to leave a message.

FMCSA Licensing and Insurance Register

The following requests for authority have been reviewed by the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (hereafter, the Administration) and are being published as preliminary grants. Some descriptions of requested service may have been modified to provide for consistency in authorities issued by the Administration. These grant decision notices do not represent authority to operate.

Amendments to the applications are generally not permitted. Once the application has been filed, the applicant may revise a request for authority or supplement evidence only with the approval of the Administration.

Applicants will be sent a letter on the day when notice of their application appears in the FMCSA Register. This letter informs them of their docket number, their insurance and process agent filing requirements and deadlines, and the publication date in the Register.

Legally sufficient opposition in the form of verified statements must be filed within 10 days from date of publication.

Opposition to a grant of operating authority will be accepted as a protest if it meets the requirement of Title 49 Code of Federal Regulations Subpart B. Protests should be sent to: Associate Administrator, Office of Research and Information Technology, FMCSA, 1200 New Jersey Avenue, SE, W65-206, Washington DC 20590.

In the absence of opposition, authorities will be issued to those applicants that, within 20 days from date of publication, have filed evidence of appropriate compliance.

Applications that are not supplemented with the required insurance and process agent filings by the 20th day following publication in the FMCSA Register will be dismissed. Dismissal notices will be issued to non-complying applicants on the 30th day after publication in the FMCSA Register.

AUTOMATED RESPONSE CAPABILITY
(ARC)

Use your touch-tone phone to call the Automated Response Capability (ARC) line 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. CALL: (202) 358-7000
When the ARC answers, you may choose from the following options:

Carrier Case Status: accesses the database to find the status of applications and case proceedings
Carrier Insurance Status: accesses the database to find carrier insurance records; also, process agent information.
How to File: explains how to file applications and obtain forms; also provides direction for assistance with complaints.
Problems or questions concerning ARC may be directed to the ARC Project Coordinator at (202) 358-7039.

WEB SITE
You may also obtain real-time information on the status of applications, insurance filings, and process agent filings by visiting our web site at: http://li-public.fmcsa.dot.gov
